**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

86-assistanttext-
The document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

**Document overview**

The guide is organized into 8 sections, all grounded in concrete file evidence:

1. **Purpose and Boundaries** — positions the container manager between the kubelet's scheduling layer and the Linux kernel's cgroup interface, identifies upstream (kubelet, cAdvisor) and downstream (CRI, device plugin gRPC, DRA gRPC) dependencies.

2. **Key Components** — explains the 11 main components with their responsibilities:
   - `ContainerManager` interface and its `NodeConfig` configuration carrier
   - `containerManagerImpl` (Linux) with its initialization dependency order (topology manager must precede all hint providers)
   - `CgroupManager` and the cgroupfs vs. systemd driver path translation
   - `QOSContainerManager` — the three-tier cgroup hierarchy and its periodic update
   - `PodContainerManager` — per-pod cgroup lifecycle
   - `InternalContainerLifecycle` — the three CRI hook points (`PreCreateContainer`, `PreStartContainer`, `PostStopContainer`) that wire resource allocations to the actual container
   - CPU Manager, Memory Manager, Topology Manager, Device Manager, DRA Manager

3. **End-to-End Flow** — traces six concrete flows: initialization, node setup, pod admission (topology manager orchestration), container start (how cpuset ends up in the CRI request), container removal, and resource status updates.

4. **Failure Modes and Tradeoffs** — covers kubelet-killing startup failures, soft requirements, the NUMA node count limit of 8, the CPU manager reconciliation gap, device plugin disconnect behavior, the silent retry loop in node allocatable enforcement, and the `CgroupsPerQOS=false` tradeoff.

5. **Extension Points** — documents the `Po

hierarchy.\\n864: \\tif cpu != memory {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", fmt.Errorf(\\\"cpu and memory cgroup hierarchy not unified.  cpu: %s, memory: %s\\\", cpu, memory)\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\t// on systemd, every pid is in a unified cgroup hierarchy (name=systemd as seen in systemd-cgls)\\n869: \\t// cpu and memory accounting is off by default, users may choose to enable it per unit or globally.\\n870: \\t// users could enable CPU and memory accounting globally via /etc/systemd/system.conf (DefaultCPUAccounting=true DefaultMemoryAccounting=true).\\n871: \\t// users could also enable CPU and memory accounting per unit via CPUAccounting=true and MemoryAccounting=true\\n872: \\t// we only warn if accounting is not enabled for CPU or memory so as to not break local development flows where kubelet is launched in a terminal.\\n873: \\t// for example, the cgroup for the user session will be something like /user.slice/user-X.slice/session-X.scope, but the cpu and memory\\n874: \\t// cgroup will be the closest ancestor where accounting is performed (most likely /) on systems that launch docker containers.\\n875: \\t// as a result, on those systems, you will not get cpu or memory accounting statistics for kubelet.\\n876: \\t// in addition, you would not get memory or cpu accounting for the runtime unless accounting was enabled on its unit (or globally).\\n877: \\tif systemd, cpu, nil\\n888: }\\n889: \\n890: // Ensures the system container is created and all non-kernel threads and process 1\\n891: // without a container are moved to it.\\n892: //\\n893: // The reason of leaving kernel threads at root cgroup is that we don't want to tie the\\n894: // execution of these threads with to-be defined /system quota and create priority inversions.\\n895: func ensureSystemCgroups(logger klog.Logger, rootCgroupPath string, manager cgroups.Manager) error {\\n896: \\t// Move non-kernel PIDs to the system container.\\n897: \\t// Only keep errors on latest attempt.\\n898: \\tvar finalErr error\\n899: \\tfor i := 0; i <= 10; i++ {\\n900: \\t\\tallPids, err := cmutil.GetPids(rootCgroupPath)\\n901: \\t\\tif err != nil {\\n902: \\t\\t\\tfinalErr = \\t\\t\\t}\\n933: \\t\\t}\\n934: \\n935: \\t}\\n936: \\n937: \\treturn finalErr\\n938: }\\n939: \\n940: // Determines whether the specified PID is a kernel PID.\\n941: func isKernelPid(pid int) bool // setupKernelTunables validates kernel tunable flags are set as expected\n457: // depending upon the specified option, it will either warn, error, or modify the kernel tunable flags\n458: func setupKernelTunables(logger klog.Logger, option KernelTunableBehavior) error {\n459: \tdesiredState := map[string]int{\n460: \t\tutilsysctl.VMOvercommitMemory: utilsysctl.VMOvercommitMemoryAlways,\n461: \t\tutilsysctl.VMPanicOnOOM:       utilsysctl.VMPanicOnOOMInvokeOOMKiller,\n462: \t\tutilsysctl.KernelPanic:        utilsysctl.KernelPanicRebootTimeout,\n463: \t\tutilsysctl.KernelPanicOnOops:  utilsysctl.KernelPanicOnOopsAlways,\n464: \t\tutilsysctl.RootMaxKeys:        utilsysctl.RootMaxKeysSetting,\n465: \t\tutilsysctl.RootMaxBytes:       utilsysctl.RootMaxBytesSetting,\n466: \t}\n467: \n468: \tsysctl := utilsysctl.New()\n469: \n470: \terrList := []error{}\n471: \tfor flag, expectedValue := range desiredState {\n472: \t\tval, err := sysctl.GetSysctl(flag)\n473: \t\tif err != nil {\n474: \t\t\terrList = append(errList, err)\n475: \t\t\tcontinue\n476: \t\t}\n477: \t\tif val == expectedValue {\n478: \t\t\tcontinue\n479: \t\t}\n480: \n481: \t\tswitch option {\n482: \t\tcase KernelTunableError:\n483: \t\t\terrList = append(errList, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid kernel flag: %v, expected value: %v, actual value: %v\", flag, expectedValue, val))\n484: \t\tcase KernelTunableWarn:\n485: \t\t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Invalid kernel flag\", \"flag\", flag, \"expectedValue\", expectedValue, \"actualValue\", val)\n486: \t\tcase KernelTunableModify:\n487: \t\t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Updating kernel flag\", \"flag\", flag, \"expectedValue\", expectedValue, \"actualValue\", val)\n488: \t\t\terr = sysctl.SetSysctl(flag, expectedValue)\n489: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n490: \t\t\t\tif inuserns.RunningInUserNS() {\n491: \t\t\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(kubefeatures.KubeletInUserNamespace) {\n492: \t\t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Updating kernel flag failed (running in UserNS, ignoring)\", \"flag\", flag, \"err\", err)\n493: \t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Updating kernel flag failed (Hint: enable KubeletInUserNamespace feature flag to ignore the error)\", \"flag\", flag)\n496: \t\t\t\t}\n497: \t\t\t\terrList = append(errList, err)\n498: \t\t\t}\n499: \t\t}\n500: \t}\n501: \treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errList)\n502: }\n503: \n504: func (cm {
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager: Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Key Components and Responsibilities](#2-key-components-and-responsibilities)\n3. [End-to-End Control Flow](#3-end-to-end-control-flow)\n4. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#4-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n5. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#5-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n6. [Platform Variance](#6-platform-variance)\n7. [Operational Implications](#7-operational-implications)\n8. [File and Directory Map](#8-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe kubelet **container manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the subsystem responsible for enforcing resource isolation on the node. It sits between the kubelet's scheduling logic and the kernel's control-group (cgroup) infrastructure, ensuring that:\n\n- Pod and container workloads are placed inside a well-defined cgroup hierarchy.\n- CPU, memory, and device resources are allocated, tracked, and released correctly for every container lifecycle event.\n- NUMA locality preferences from multiple resource domains (CPU, memory, devices) are coordinated before a container starts.\n- Node-level resource reservations (for OS and kubelet itself) are enforced.\n\n### Upstream dependencies\n\nThe container manager is constructed and owned by the kubelet proper (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`, field `containerManager cm.ContainerManager`, line 1436). The kubelet calls `containerManager.Start(...)` after cAdvisor is initialized (line 1752), because capacity figures from cAdvisor feed the initial resource calculations.\n\n### Downstream dependencies\n\n- **Linux kernel cgroup interface** \u2014 through `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` (runc's libcontainer cgroup library).\n- **CRI runtime** \u2014 the container manager's `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks inject CPU/memory affinity settings directly into the `ContainerConfig` before the CRI `CreateContainer` call is made.\n- **Device plugin gRPC endpoints** \u2014 the device manager opens a plugin API server that device plugins connect to at `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`.\n- **DRA driver gRPC endpoints** \u2014 the DRA manager communicates with resource driver plugins via a watcher mechanism.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `ContainerManager` Interface\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`\n\nThe public contract surface used by the kubelet. The interface has three main responsibility clusters:\n\n| Cluster | Selected methods |\n|---|---|\n| Node-level cgroup setup | `Start`, `SystemCgroupsLimit`, `GetPodCgroupRoot`, `GetMountedSubsystems` |\n| Resource capacity and allocation | `GetCapacity`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation`, `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity`, `GetResources`, `UpdatePluginResources` |\n| Dynamic resources and updates | `PrepareDynamicResources`, `UnprepareDynamicResources`, `Updates()` |\n\nThe interface also embeds the four `podresources` provider interfaces (`CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider`), making `containerManagerImpl` directly usable as the data source for the PodResources gRPC API.\n\nThe `NodeConfig` struct (lines 176\u2013202) is the configuration carrier: it contains the cgroup root, driver type, QoS per-pod flag, CPU/memory manager policy names, topology manager policy, and all node allocatable settings.\n\n### 2.2 `containerManagerImpl` \u2014 Linux Implementation\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`\n\nThe concrete struct that satisfies `ContainerManager` on Linux. It holds references to every sub-manager:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl {\n    cadvisorInterface     // hardware metrics\n    cgroupManager         // raw cgroup CRUD\n    qosContainerManager   // QoS tier cgroups\n    deviceManager         // device plugin protocol\n    cpuManager            // CPU affinity / pinning\n    memoryManager         // memory NUMA affinity\n    topologyManager       // NUMA alignment coordinator\n    draManager            // Dynamic Resource Allocation\n    resourceUpdates chan   // fan-in update channel for device/DRA events\n}\n```\n\n`NewContainerManager` (line 207) performs construction in a fixed order: cgroup detection \u2192 swap detection \u2192 capacity via cAdvisor \u2192 topology manager \u2192 device manager \u2192 DRA manager \u2192 CPU manager \u2192 memory manager. The topology manager must exist before device, CPU, and memory managers because each of those calls `topologyManager.AddHintProvider(...)` to register itself.\n\nA goroutine fan-in loop (lines 363\u2013389) merges resource-status update channels from the device manager and DRA manager into a single `cm.resourceUpdates` channel. The kubelet consumes this channel to trigger pod status refreshes.\n\n### 2.3 `CgroupManager` Interface\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` (shared logic), `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` / `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` (versioned implementations)\n\nThe lowest-level cgroup abstraction: creates, destroys, updates, and queries cgroup directories. The two concrete implementations differ primarily in how they translate the abstract `CgroupName` type into filesystem paths:\n\n- **cgroupfs driver**: paths are slash-joined directory components under the cgroup mountpoint (e.g., `/sys/fs/cgroup/kubepods/burstable/pod<uid>`).\n- **systemd driver**: names are escaped using the `CgroupName.ToSystemd()` conversion (line 81 of `cgroup_manager_linux.go`), producing systemd slice notation like `kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/...`. The `-` character in pod UIDs is remapped to `_` to preserve round-trip convertibility.\n\n`NewCgroupManager` (called from `NewContainerManager`) selects the implementation based on `NodeConfig.CgroupDriver` and returns either the v1 or v2 manager depending on `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`.\n\nThe v2 manager (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`, `cgroupV2impl`) operates on the unified hierarchy \u2014 all controller files exist in a single directory \u2014 and uses the `cpu.max` and `memory.max` interfaces instead of the v1 `cpu.cfs_quota_us` / `memory.limit_in_bytes` files.\n\n### 2.4 `QOSContainerManager`\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`\n\nWhen `CgroupsPerQOS: true`, this component maintains the three-tier cgroup hierarchy directly under the allocatable cgroup root:\n\n```\nkubepods/               \u2190 node allocatable root\n  burstable/            \u2190 Burstable QoS class\n  besteffort/           \u2190 BestEffort QoS class\n  (Guaranteed pods are direct children of kubepods/)\n```\n\nIt periodically (every 1 minute, `periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`) recalculates CPU and memory limits for the `burstable` tier by summing the resources of all active Burstable pods. The BestEffort tier is statically set to the kernel minimum CPU shares (`MinShares = 2`). Guaranteed pods have no QoS-level cgroup \u2014 they sit directly under the kubepods root (since they declare exact CPU/memory).\n\n### 2.5 `PodContainerManager`\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` (Linux implementation), `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_stub.go` (no-op)\n\nOne level below the QoS tier, each pod gets its own cgroup named `pod<uid>`. The `EnsureExists` method (line 74) creates this cgroup on first use and applies per-pod resource parameters via `ResourceConfigForPod`. Features like `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` are checked here: if a pod has exclusively pinned CPUs via the CPU manager, CFS quota enforcement is suppressed at the pod cgroup level to avoid double accounting.\n\nThe `podContainerManagerImpl` is not a singleton. Each call to `containerManager.NewPodContainerManager()` creates a new value that captures the current QoS cgroup info at that moment.\n\n### 2.6 `InternalContainerLifecycle`\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` (interface and cross-platform impl), `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` (Linux-specific pre-create hook)\n\nThis interface is the bridge between the container manager and the CRI runtime call path in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_container.go`. It has three hooks called by the kuberuntime manager:\n\n| Hook | Where called | What it does |\n|---|---|---|\n| `PreCreateContainer` | Before `CreateContainer` RPC | Writes `cpuset_cpus` and `cpuset_mems` into the `ContainerConfig.Linux.Resources` based on CPU manager and memory manager allocations |\n| `PreStartContainer` | After `CreateContainer`, before `StartContainer` | Calls `cpuManager.AddContainer`, `memoryManager.AddContainer`, and `topologyManager.AddContainer` to register the live container ID |\n| `PostStopContainer` | After `StopContainer` | Calls `topologyManager.RemoveContainer` to release the NUMA affinity entry |\n\nThe `PreCreateContainer` hook (in `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go`) is where CPU pinning becomes real: it calls `cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity(podUID, containerName)` and writes the resulting cpuset string directly into the CRI request.\n\n### 2.7 CPU Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, `policy.go`, `policy_static.go`, `policy_none.go`\n\nThe CPU manager controls `cpuset.cpus` affinity for containers. It supports two policies:\n\n**`none` policy** \u2014 no exclusive allocation. All containers share all CPUs.\n\n**`static` policy** (`policy_static.go`) \u2014 Guaranteed pods whose CPU request is a positive integer receive exclusive CPU cores, isolated from the shared pool. The policy maintains three logical sets:\n\n- **SHARED**: all CPUs minus exclusively allocated ones. Burstable and BestEffort pods run here.\n- **RESERVED**: a subset of SHARED not available for exclusive allocation, sized to `ceil(systemreserved.cpu + kubereserved.cpu)`.\n- **ASSIGNABLE**: SHARED minus RESERVED. Exclusive allocations are drawn from here.\n\nState is checkpointed to disk at `{kubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state` so that allocations survive kubelet restarts. A reconcile loop (period configurable via `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod`) periodically calls `UpdateContainerResources` on the CRI to re-apply cpuset assignments, handling drift caused by container restarts.\n\nThe CPU manager implements `topologymanager.HintProvider` so the topology manager can incorporate CPU NUMA affinity when choosing an allocation.\n\n### 2.8 Memory Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`, `policy_static.go`, `policy_none.go`\n\nAnalogous to the CPU manager but for huge-page and regular memory NUMA affinity. The static policy allocates memory blocks from specific NUMA nodes for Guaranteed pods and sets `cpuset.mems` accordingly (written via `PreCreateContainer`). State is checkpointed to `{kubeletRootDir}/memory_manager_state`. Like the CPU manager it is a `topologymanager.HintProvider`.\n\n### 2.9 Topology Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`, `scope.go`, `scope_container.go`, `scope_pod.go`, `policy_*.go`\n\nThe topology manager is a **coordinator**, not an allocator. Its job is to ensure that when multiple resource providers (CPU manager, memory manager, device manager) each have NUMA locality preferences, the final allocation is globally consistent.\n\nIt implements `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`, meaning it participates in pod admission (returned via `cm.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`). During admission it:\n\n1. Asks each registered `HintProvider` for its set of `TopologyHint` values (NUMA node bitmasks, each tagged as preferred or not).\n2. Merges hints using the configured policy.\n3. Stores the winning `TopologyHint` per container.\n4. Calls `Allocate` on each `HintProvider` to trigger actual resource allocation consistent with the chosen affinity.\n\nFour policies are supported: `none`, `best-effort`, `restricted`, `single-numa-node`. Two scopes exist: `container` (per-container alignment) and `pod` (all containers in a pod share the same NUMA domain). The maximum supported NUMA node count is 8 (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes`, line 41 of `topology_manager.go`) due to state-space explosion in hint enumeration.\n\n### 2.10 Device Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`, `endpoint.go`, `pod_devices.go`\n\nManages the Device Plugin API. Device plugins register themselves by connecting to the kubelet's plugin watcher socket (`pluginwatcherapi.DevicePlugin`). The device manager:\n\n- Tracks healthy and unhealthy devices per resource name.\n- During pod admission, calls `Allocate` on device plugin endpoints to reserve devices.\n- Returns `RunContainerOptions` (devices, mounts, environment variables, annotations, CDI device IDs) for injection into container configuration.\n- Checkpoints allocated device-to-container mappings to survive kubelet restarts.\n- Pushes `resourceupdates.Update` events when device health changes, enabling the kubelet to refresh pod status.\n\nThe device manager also implements `topologymanager.HintProvider`, contributing NUMA node affinity hints based on which NUMA node a physical device is attached to.\n\n### 2.11 DRA Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`, `claiminfo.go`, `healthinfo.go`\n\nThe Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) manager handles `ResourceClaim` objects \u2014 a newer, more expressive alternative to the Device Plugin API that requires the `DynamicResourceAllocation` feature gate. Unlike device plugins, DRA drivers communicate via structured API calls (`drapb` protobuf) rather than environment variables and device files.\n\n`PrepareDynamicResources` and `UnprepareDynamicResources` are called by the kubelet's pod lifecycle before and after containers run. The manager checkpoints claim state to `{kubeletRootDir}/dra_manager_state`. When `ResourceHealthStatus` feature gate is also enabled, the DRA manager sends health update events through its `Updates()` channel which is merged into the container manager's fan-in `resourceUpdates` channel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Initialization\n\n```\nkubelet.go: NewMainKubelet()\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 cm.NewContainerManager(ctx, mountUtil, cadvisor, nodeConfig, ...)\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 GetCgroupSubsystems() \u2192 detects mounted cgroup hierarchies\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 swap.IsSwapOn() \u2192 decides if swap should fail or warn\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 cadvisor.MachineInfo() \u2192 CPU topology, memory, NUMA nodes\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 NewCgroupManager() \u2192 selects cgroupfs or systemd driver, v1 or v2\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 NewQOSContainerManager() \u2192 sets up burstable/besteffort cgroup info\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 topologymanager.NewManager() \u2192 reads NUMA topology, creates scope\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 devicemanager.NewManagerImpl() \u2192 registers as topology hint provider\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 dra.NewManager() \u2192 (if DynamicResourceAllocation gate enabled)\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpumanager.NewManager() \u2192 loads state checkpoint, registers as hint provider\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 memorymanager.NewManager() \u2192 loads state checkpoint, registers as hint provider\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 starts goroutine fan-in for resourceUpdates channel\n```\n\n### 3.2 Node Setup (Start)\n\n```\nkubelet.go: Run() \u2192 containerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, ...)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime() \u2192 snapshot of running containers from CRI\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 draManager.Start() \u2192 begins reconcile loop for ResourceClaims\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.Start() \u2192 restores allocations from checkpoint, starts reconcile goroutine\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.Start() \u2192 restores allocations from checkpoint, starts reconcile goroutine\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 cadvisor.RootFsInfo() \u2192 populates ephemeral storage capacity\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 validateNodeAllocatable() \u2192 sanity check on reserved vs. total resources\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 setupNode(ctx, activePods):\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 validateSystemRequirements() \u2192 checks cgroup subsystems are mounted\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 setupKernelTunables() \u2192 vm.overcommit_memory, kernel.panic, etc.\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 createNodeAllocatableCgroups() \u2192 ensures kubepods cgroup exists\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 qosContainerManager.Start() \u2192 creates burstable/besteffort tiers\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups() \u2192 applies memory/CPU limits on kubepods, kube-reserved, system-reserved\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 configures systemContainers (system cgroup, kubelet cgroup)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.Start() \u2192 starts gRPC plugin server, registers watcher handler\n```\n\n### 3.3 Pod Admission\n\nWhen the kubelet's predicate admission handler fires (in `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`), the topology manager's `Admit` method runs:\n\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 for each HintProvider (cpuManager, memoryManager, deviceManager):\n  \u2502     GetTopologyHints(pod, container) \u2192 []TopologyHint (NUMA bitmasks)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 mergeTopologyHints() \u2192 select best affinity per configured policy\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 store affinity per (podUID, containerName)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 for each HintProvider:\n        Allocate(pod, container) \u2192 reserve resources consistent with affinity\n              cpuManager: assign CPU set in state\n              memoryManager: assign memory block in state\n              deviceManager: call device plugin Allocate RPC\n```\n\nIf the topology manager's policy is `restricted` or `single-numa-node` and no feasible alignment exists, `Admit` returns a rejection with type `TopologyAffinityError`.\n\nFor DRA resources, `PrepareDynamicResources` is called separately by the pod worker before containers start.\n\n### 3.4 Container Start\n\n```\nkuberuntime_container.go: startContainer(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 internalLifecycle.PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity() \u2192 write cpuset_cpus into ContainerConfig\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() \u2192 write cpuset_mems into ContainerConfig\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 draManager.GetResources() \u2192 CDI device IDs\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() \u2192 devices, mounts, envs, CDI devices\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 podContainerManager.EnsureExists(pod) \u2192 create/verify pod cgroup\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 CRI: CreateContainer(containerConfig) \u2190 CPU/memory affinity already embedded\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 internalLifecycle.PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.AddContainer() \u2192 register containerID\u2192(podUID, name) mapping\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.AddContainer() \u2192 same\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologyManager.AddContainer() \u2192 same\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 CRI: StartContainer(containerID)\n```\n\n### 3.5 Container Removal\n\n```\nkuberuntime_container.go: killContainer(containerID)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 CRI: StopContainer()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 internalLifecycle.PostStopContainer(containerID)\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologyManager.RemoveContainer() \u2192 frees affinity record\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.RemoveContainer() \u2192 returns CPUs to shared pool\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.RemoveContainer() \u2192 returns memory blocks to pool\n```\n\nThe pod cgroup is cleaned up asynchronously via `podContainerManager.Destroy()` after all containers in the pod have stopped.\n\n### 3.6 Resource Status Updates\n\nDevice health changes (device goes offline or recovers) propagate via:\n\n```\ndeviceManager updates channel \u2192 containerManagerImpl.resourceUpdates channel\n                                    \u2192 kubelet sync loop\n                                       \u2192 podStatusManager updates pod status\n```\n\nThis is the same channel path for DRA health events when `ResourceHealthStatus` is enabled.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Startup failures that kill the kubelet\n\n`containerManager.Start` failures cause `os.Exit(1)` in the kubelet (line 1755, `kubelet.go`). The following conditions cause this:\n\n- Required cgroup subsystems (`cpu`, `cpuacct`, `cpuset`, `memory` on v1) are not mounted.\n- The cgroup root specified by `--cgroup-root` does not exist.\n- Swap is on and `--fail-swap-on` is true.\n- CPU manager or memory manager fail to restore from checkpoint (e.g., checkpoint file is corrupted).\n\n### Soft requirements\n\nIf CPU hard-capping (CFS quota) is not available (v1 without `cpu.cfs_quota_us`), `containerManagerImpl.status.SoftRequirements` is set to an error. The kubelet continues but reports this degraded state via `containerManager.Status()`. CPU limits on containers are then advisory-only.\n\n### cgroup v1 deprecation warning\n\nSince v1 support is explicitly deprecated, `NewContainerManager` emits `CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning` (line 52, `container_manager.go`) on startup when v1 is detected.\n\n### Topology manager NUMA explosion limit\n\nThe topology manager caps supported NUMA nodes at 8 (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes`). Beyond that, the combinatorial space of possible NUMA bitmasks becomes too large. On machines with more NUMA nodes, the topology manager refuses to start.\n\n### CPU manager reconciliation gap\n\nBetween container admission (when the CPU set is written to state) and `PreStartContainer` (when the container ID is registered), there is a window where the cpuset may not be applied to the actual container process. The reconcile loop closes this gap but introduces a latency equal to `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` (default 10 seconds) for out-of-sync detection.\n\n### Device plugin disconnect\n\nWhen a device plugin disconnects, the device manager marks its devices as unhealthy but retains the plugin's endpoint for a grace period. Pods that already hold allocations from a disconnected plugin are not immediately evicted, but new pods cannot request that resource type until the plugin reconnects.\n\n### QoS cgroup memory updates on a loaded node\n\nWhen `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups` cannot apply memory limits immediately (because existing pod memory usage exceeds the new limit), it retries in a goroutine indefinitely with a 1-minute sleep (`node_container_manager_linux.go`, lines 95\u2013107). This means a node that is already over-committed on memory will loop silently until eviction frees enough memory to satisfy the limit.\n\n### Tradeoff: CgroupsPerQOS = false\n\nWith `CgroupsPerQOS: false`, the QoS cgroup tier does not exist and `NewPodContainerManager()` returns a no-op stub (`podContainerManagerNoop`). This removes the ability to enforce per-QoS memory reservations but eliminates cgroup management overhead, which matters on nodes with very large numbers of pods.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policies\n\n**Interface:** `cpumanager.Policy` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go`)  \n**Built-in implementations:** `none`, `static`\n\nThe `Policy` interface (`Name`, `Start`, `Allocate`, `RemoveContainer`, `GetTopologyHints`, `GetPodTopologyHints`, `GetAllocatableCPUs`) is the intended extension point for custom CPU allocation strategies. The `static` policy supports named options (`CPUManagerPolicyOptions`) such as `full-pcpus-only` and `distribute-cpus-across-numa`, selected at kubelet startup time.\n\n**Risk:** A custom policy that mismanages state (e.g., double-frees CPU sets or fails to checkpoint) will corrupt the in-memory cpuset assignment and may cause containers to compete for the same physical CPUs.\n\n### 5.2 Memory Manager Policies\n\n**Interface:** `memorymanager.Manager` and embedded `Policy` type (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go`)  \n**Built-in implementations:** `None`, `Static`\n\nAnalogous to the CPU manager. The `None` policy is a pass-through. The `Static` policy enforces NUMA memory affinity for Guaranteed pods.\n\n### 5.3 Topology Manager Policies and Scopes\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_*.go`, `scope_*.go`\n\nFour policies (`none`, `best-effort`, `restricted`, `single-numa-node`) and two scopes (`container`, `pod`) are selectable via `--topology-manager-policy` and `--topology-manager-scope`. Policies can also take per-option maps (`TopologyManagerPolicyOptions`).\n\nAdding a new policy means implementing the `Policy` interface from `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy.go` and registering it in `NewManager`. Incorrect policy logic that ignores `Preferred: false` hints can silently relax NUMA constraints, which shows up only as degraded memory bandwidth at runtime.\n\n### 5.4 Device Plugin Registration\n\nThe device manager exposes a gRPC plugin server that any in-cluster device plugin binary can connect to. There is no code extension needed in the container manager itself \u2014 plugins register themselves at runtime by connecting to the kubelet socket (`pluginwatcherapi.DevicePlugin`). The device manager's watcher handler is returned by `cm.GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` and integrated into the plugin manager.\n\n**Risk:** A device plugin that incorrectly reports topology (e.g., wrong NUMA node affiliation) will cause the topology manager to make suboptimal or invalid NUMA alignments for workloads requesting that device.\n\n### 5.5 DRA Driver Registration\n\nDRA drivers register via `pluginwatcherapi.DRAPlugin`. The `draManager.GetWatcherHandler()` implements the same `cache.PluginHandler` interface used by device plugins, enabling the existing plugin infrastructure to route registrations to the DRA manager. DRA drivers communicate with more structure than device plugins: they use the `drapb` protobuf API.\n\n### 5.6 `containerManagerStub` for Testing\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go`\n\nA full no-op implementation of `ContainerManager` used in unit tests and the hollow kubelet (`pkg/kubemark`). It initializes fake CPU and memory managers (`cpumanager.NewFakeManager`, `memorymanager.NewFakeManager`) so `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks still execute without panicking.\n\n### 5.7 Kernel Tunable Behavior\n\n`setupKernelTunables` accepts a `KernelTunableBehavior` enum (`warn`, `error`, `modify`). The default is `modify` (the kubelet adjusts sysctls like `vm.overcommit_memory` on its own). If `--protect-kernel-defaults` is set the behavior switches to `error`, which will block kubelet startup if the host kernel parameters do not match expected values. This is an operational extension point for hardened environments.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Platform Variance\n\n### Linux (primary)\n\nFull functionality. The `containerManagerImpl` struct in `container_manager_linux.go` implements the complete interface:\n\n- cgroup v1 or v2 hierarchy via `cgroupV1impl` / `cgroupV2impl`\n- QoS cgroup tiers, pod cgroups\n- CPU manager with `static` policy (CPU pinning via cpuset)\n- Memory manager with NUMA affinity\n- Topology manager\n- Device manager with device plugin API\n- DRA manager (feature gated)\n- Kernel tunable management\n- OOM score adjustment for the kubelet process itself (`ensureProcessInContainerWithOOMScore`)\n\n**cgroup v2 differences:** The v2 manager uses the unified hierarchy under `/sys/fs/cgroup`. Memory QoS (`MemoryQoS` feature gate) is only enabled on v2 and uses `memory.min` (guaranteed minimum) and `memory.high` (soft limit) instead of just `memory.limit_in_bytes`. CPU quota uses `cpu.max` (a single file with `quota period` format) rather than two separate files.\n\n### Windows\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go`\n\nThe Windows `containerManagerImpl` struct contains `deviceManager`, `topologyManager`, `cpuManager`, and `memoryManager` fields, meaning device plugin and topology-aware resource allocation work on Windows. However, there is no cgroup infrastructure: QoS containers, pod cgroups, and node allocatable enforcement are not implemented. Methods like `GetQOSContainersInfo`, `GetMountedSubsystems`, and `GetPodCgroupRoot` return empty/stub values.\n\n### Unsupported / Stub (non-Linux, non-Windows)\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_unsupported.go` (builds on platforms other than linux/windows)\n\nReturns an error from `NewContainerManager`. The stub (`container_manager_stub.go`) is used in test builds on any platform.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**cgroup write overhead:** Every pod start triggers at minimum one `cgroupManager.Create` call (pod cgroup) plus `cgroupManager.Update` calls for the QoS tier. On nodes with many short-lived pods (e.g., batch jobs), this can become measurable I/O contention on the cgroup filesystem. The v2 unified hierarchy reduces per-operation syscalls compared to v1 (which requires one write per subsystem mount).\n\n**CPU manager reconciliation CPU cost:** The reconcile loop calls `UpdateContainerResources` on the CRI for every container that has drifted from its expected cpuset. On nodes with many guaranteed pods, this loop can issue hundreds of CRI calls per reconcile period. Tuning `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` higher reduces overhead but increases the window in which a container runs on wrong CPUs after a restart.\n\n**Topology hint computation:** At pod admission, the topology manager collects hints from all providers and computes their intersection. The cost grows with the number of NUMA nodes (exponential in the number of possible bitmasks) and the number of registered hint providers. For the common case (2\u20134 NUMA nodes, 3 providers), this is negligible, but it becomes a bottleneck on 8-node NUMA machines under admission pressure.\n\n### Reliability\n\n**Checkpoint durability:** The CPU manager, memory manager, and device manager all checkpoint allocation state to files in `KubeletRootDir`. If the checkpoint file is lost (e.g., the directory is on a volatile tmpfs), the manager cannot reconcile pre-existing allocations after a kubelet restart and may over-allocate or under-allocate resources. Best practice is to use a persistent `--root-dir`.\n\n**QoS cgroup update retry loop:** As described in \u00a74, the node allocatable enforcement goroutine (`enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups`) silently retries indefinitely. There is no circuit breaker or alertable metric on this path, making it operationally invisible unless the node's events are monitored (`FailedNodeAllocatableEnforcement` and `SuccessfulNodeAllocatableEnforcement` event reasons).\n\n**Device manager health tracking:** The `Updates()` channel propagates health changes to the kubelet's pod status machinery. If the kubelet's main sync loop is backed up (e.g., due to a slow API server), device health events queue in the buffered `resourceUpdates` channel (capacity 10, line 360 of `container_manager_linux.go`). In extreme cases this can delay pod status transitions.\n\n### Maintainability\n\nThe Linux implementation tightly couples three concerns in `containerManagerImpl`: cgroup hierarchy management, resource manager lifecycle, and node allocatable accounting. The `// TODO: move the GetResources logic to PodContainerManager` comment on line 728 of `container_manager_linux.go` reflects acknowledged technical debt. Over time, the Linux file has grown to >1100 lines and mixes initialization, periodic tasks, and per-container request serving.\n\nThe use of build tags (`//go:build linux`, `//go:build windows`) for platform variance rather than interface dispatch means adding a new platform requires duplicating significant struct and method scaffolding. The stub/Windows implementations show that this has already led to divergence in what sub-managers are initialized.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | `ContainerManager` interface definition; `NodeConfig`; helper functions for resource parsing and device topology serialization |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux `containerManagerImpl`; `NewContainerManager`; `Start`; fan-in of resource update channels; per-container resource helpers |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows `containerManagerImpl`; partial implementation (no cgroup hierarchy) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go` | No-op stub for tests and hollow kubelet; `NewStubContainerManager` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | `CgroupManager`, `PodContainerManager`, `QOSContainersInfo`, `ResourceConfig`, `CgroupConfig`, `CgroupName` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` | `CgroupName` path conversion (cgroupfs and systemd); `NewCgroupManager`; shared v1/v2 logic |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` | cgroup v1 implementation of `CgroupManager` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` | cgroup v2 implementation of `CgroupManager` (`cgroupV2impl`) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` | `QOSContainerManager`; burstable/besteffort tier creation; periodic QoS cgroup update |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` | `podContainerManagerImpl`; per-pod cgroup creation via `EnsureExists` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/node_container_manager_linux.go` | Node allocatable cgroup enforcement; kube-reserved and system-reserved cgroup limits |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` | `InternalContainerLifecycle` interface; `PreStartContainer`, `PostStopContainer` implementations |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` | `PreCreateContainer`; injects `cpuset_cpus` / `cpuset_mems` into CRI `ContainerConfig` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go` | `MilliCPUToQuota`, `ResourceConfigForPod`, `MinShares`, `SharesPerCPU`, conversion constants |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` | `cpumanager.Manager` interface; `manager` struct; reconcile loop |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go` | `Policy` interface |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_static.go` | Static CPU policy; SHARED/RESERVED/ASSIGNABLE set logic; NUMA node limit constant |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/scope.go` | `Scope` interface; admission orchestration |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_*.go` | `none`, `best-effort`, `restricted`, `single-numa-node` policies |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go` | `ManagerImpl`; device plugin gRPC server; allocation state |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/pod_devices.go` | Allocation state keyed by (pod, container, resource); checkpoint serialization |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go` | DRA `Manager`; ResourceClaim prepare/unprepare; DRA plugin watcher |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/state/` | Checkpoint state for DRA claim assignments |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/resourceupdates/updates.go` | `Update` struct (PodUIDs); {
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager: Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Key Components and Responsibilities](#2-key-components-and-responsibilities)\n3. [End-to-End Control Flow](#3-end-to-end-control-flow)\n4. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#4-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n5. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#5-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n6. [Platform Variance](#6-platform-variance)\n7. [Operational Implications](#7-operational-implications)\n8. [File and Directory Map](#8-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe kubelet **container manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the subsystem responsible for enforcing resource isolation on the node. It sits between the kubelet's scheduling logic and the kernel's control-group (cgroup) infrastructure, ensuring that:\n\n- Pod and container workloads are placed inside a well-defined cgroup hierarchy.\n- CPU, memory, and device resources are allocated, tracked, and released correctly for every container lifecycle event.\n- NUMA locality preferences from multiple resource domains (CPU, memory, devices) are coordinated before a container starts.\n- Node-level resource reservations (for OS and the kubelet itself) are enforced.\n\n### Upstream dependencies\n\nThe container manager is constructed and owned by the kubelet proper (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`, field `containerManager cm.ContainerManager`, line 1436). The kubelet calls `containerManager.Start(...)` after cAdvisor is initialized (line 1752), because capacity figures from cAdvisor feed the initial resource calculations.\n\n### Downstream dependencies\n\n- **Linux kernel cgroup interface** \u2014 through `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` (runc's libcontainer cgroup library).\n- **CRI runtime** \u2014 the container manager's `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks inject CPU/memory affinity settings directly into the `ContainerConfig` before the CRI `CreateContainer` call is made.\n- **Device plugin gRPC endpoints** \u2014 the device manager opens a plugin API server that device plugins connect to at the kubelet plugin socket.\n- **DRA driver gRPC endpoints** \u2014 the DRA manager communicates with resource driver plugins via a watcher mechanism.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `ContainerManager` Interface\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`\n\nThe public contract surface used by the kubelet. The interface has three main responsibility clusters:\n\n| Cluster | Selected methods |\n|---|---|\n| Node-level cgroup setup | `Start`, `SystemCgroupsLimit`, `GetPodCgroupRoot`, `GetMountedSubsystems` |\n| Resource capacity and allocation | `GetCapacity`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation`, `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity`, `GetResources`, `UpdatePluginResources` |\n| Dynamic resources and updates | `PrepareDynamicResources`, `UnprepareDynamicResources`, `Updates()` |\n\nThe interface also embeds the four `podresources` provider interfaces (`CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider`), making `containerManagerImpl` directly usable as the data source for the PodResources gRPC API.\n\nThe `NodeConfig` struct (lines 176\u2013202) is the configuration carrier: it holds the cgroup root, driver type, QoS-per-pod flag, CPU/memory manager policy names, topology manager policy, and all node allocatable settings.\n\n### 2.2 `containerManagerImpl` \u2014 Linux Implementation\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`\n\nThe concrete struct that satisfies `ContainerManager` on Linux. It holds references to every sub-manager:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl {\n    cadvisorInterface     // hardware metrics\n    cgroupManager         // raw cgroup CRUD\n    qosContainerManager   // QoS tier cgroups\n    deviceManager         // device plugin protocol\n    cpuManager            // CPU affinity / pinning\n    memoryManager         // memory NUMA affinity\n    topologyManager       // NUMA alignment coordinator\n    draManager            // Dynamic Resource Allocation\n    resourceUpdates chan   // fan-in update channel for device/DRA events\n}\n```\n\n`NewContainerManager` (line 207) performs construction in a fixed order: cgroup detection \u2192 swap detection \u2192 capacity via cAdvisor \u2192 topology manager \u2192 device manager \u2192 DRA manager \u2192 CPU manager \u2192 memory manager. The topology manager must exist before the device, CPU, and memory managers because each of those calls `topologyManager.AddHintProvider(...)` during their own construction.\n\nA goroutine fan-in loop (lines 363\u2013389) merges resource-status update channels from the device manager and DRA manager into a single `cm.resourceUpdates` channel (buffered at 10). The kubelet consumes this channel to trigger pod status refreshes.\n\n### 2.3 `CgroupManager` Interface\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` (shared logic), `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` / `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` (versioned implementations)\n\nThe lowest-level cgroup abstraction: creates, destroys, updates, and queries cgroup directories. The two concrete implementations differ primarily in how they translate the abstract `CgroupName` type into filesystem paths:\n\n- **cgroupfs driver**: paths are slash-joined directory components under the cgroup mountpoint (e.g., `/sys/fs/cgroup/kubepods/burstable/pod<uid>`).\n- **systemd driver**: names are escaped using `CgroupName.ToSystemd()` (line 81 of `cgroup_manager_linux.go`), producing systemd slice notation like `kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/...`. The `-` character in pod UIDs is remapped to `_` to preserve round-trip convertibility.\n\n`NewCgroupManager` (called from `NewContainerManager`) selects the implementation based on `NodeConfig.CgroupDriver` and returns either the v1 or v2 manager depending on `cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`.\n\nThe v2 manager (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`, `cgroupV2impl`) operates on the unified hierarchy \u2014 all controller files exist in a single directory \u2014 and uses `cpu.max` and `memory.max` instead of the v1 `cpu.cfs_quota_us` / `memory.limit_in_bytes` files.\n\n### 2.4 `QOSContainerManager`\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`\n\nWhen `CgroupsPerQOS: true`, this component maintains the three-tier cgroup hierarchy directly under the allocatable cgroup root:\n\n```\nkubepods/               \u2190 node allocatable root\n  burstable/            \u2190 Burstable QoS class\n  besteffort/           \u2190 BestEffort QoS class\n  (Guaranteed pods are direct children of kubepods/)\n```\n\nIt runs a periodic update (every 1 minute, `periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`, line 45) that recalculates CPU and memory limits for the `burstable` tier by summing resources of all active Burstable pods. The BestEffort tier is statically set to the kernel minimum CPU shares (`MinShares = 2`). Guaranteed pods have no QoS-level cgroup \u2014 they sit directly under the kubepods root.\n\n### 2.5 `PodContainerManager`\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` (Linux), `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_stub.go` (no-op)\n\nOne level below the QoS tier, each pod gets its own cgroup named `pod<uid>`. The `EnsureExists` method (line 74) creates this cgroup on first use and applies per-pod resource parameters via `ResourceConfigForPod`. Features like `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` are checked here: if a pod has exclusively pinned CPUs via the CPU manager, CFS quota enforcement is suppressed at the pod cgroup level to avoid double accounting.\n\n`NewPodContainerManager()` is a factory that captures the current QoS cgroup layout at the moment of the call. When `CgroupsPerQOS` is false it returns `podContainerManagerNoop`, a no-op that skips all cgroup management.\n\n### 2.6 `InternalContainerLifecycle`\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` (interface and cross-platform impl), `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` (Linux-specific pre-create hook)\n\nThis interface is the bridge between the container manager and the CRI runtime call path in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_container.go`. It defines three hooks:\n\n| Hook | Where called | What it does |\n|---|---|---|\n| `PreCreateContainer` | Before `CreateContainer` RPC | Writes `cpuset_cpus` and `cpuset_mems` into `ContainerConfig.Linux.Resources` based on CPU manager and memory manager allocations |\n| `PreStartContainer` | After `CreateContainer`, before `StartContainer` | Calls `cpuManager.AddContainer`, `memoryManager.AddContainer`, and `topologyManager.AddContainer` to register the live container ID |\n| `PostStopContainer` | After `StopContainer` | Calls `topologyManager.RemoveContainer` to free the NUMA affinity entry |\n\nThe `PreCreateContainer` hook (in `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go`) is where CPU pinning becomes real: it calls `cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity(podUID, containerName)` and writes the resulting cpuset string directly into the CRI request before the container is created.\n\n### 2.7 CPU Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`, `policy.go`, `policy_static.go`, `policy_none.go`\n\nThe CPU manager controls `cpuset.cpus` affinity for containers. It supports two built-in policies:\n\n**`none` policy** \u2014 no exclusive allocation. All containers share all CPUs.\n\n**`static` policy** (`policy_static.go`) \u2014 Guaranteed pods whose CPU request is a positive integer receive exclusive CPU cores, isolated from the shared pool. The policy maintains three logical sets:\n\n- **SHARED**: all CPUs minus exclusively allocated ones. Burstable and BestEffort pods run here.\n- **RESERVED**: a subset of SHARED not available for exclusive allocation, sized to `ceil(systemreserved.cpu + kubereserved.cpu)`.\n- **ASSIGNABLE**: SHARED minus RESERVED. Exclusive allocations are drawn from here.\n\nState is checkpointed to `{kubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state` so allocations survive kubelet restarts. A reconcile loop (period configurable via `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod`) periodically calls `UpdateContainerResources` on the CRI to re-apply cpuset assignments and handle drift caused by container restarts.\n\nThe CPU manager implements `topologymanager.HintProvider` so the topology manager can incorporate CPU NUMA affinity when choosing an allocation.\n\n### 2.8 Memory Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`, `policy_static.go`, `policy_none.go`\n\nAnalogous to the CPU manager but for huge-page and regular memory NUMA affinity. The `static` policy allocates memory blocks from specific NUMA nodes for Guaranteed pods and sets `cpuset.mems` accordingly (written via `PreCreateContainer`). State is checkpointed to `{kubeletRootDir}/memory_manager_state`. Like the CPU manager it is a `topologymanager.HintProvider`.\n\n### 2.9 Topology Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`, `scope.go`, `scope_container.go`, `scope_pod.go`, `policy_*.go`\n\nThe topology manager is a **coordinator**, not an allocator. Its job is to ensure that when multiple resource providers (CPU manager, memory manager, device manager) each have NUMA locality preferences, the final allocation is globally consistent.\n\nIt implements `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler`, participating in pod admission (returned via `cm.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`). During admission it:\n\n1. Asks each registered `HintProvider` for its set of `TopologyHint` values (NUMA node bitmasks, each tagged as preferred or not).\n2. Merges hints using the configured policy.\n3. Stores the winning `TopologyHint` per container.\n4. Calls `Allocate` on each `HintProvider` to trigger actual resource allocation consistent with the chosen affinity.\n\nFour policies are supported: `none`, `best-effort`, `restricted`, `single-numa-node`. Two scopes exist: `container` (per-container alignment) and `pod` (all containers in a pod share the same NUMA domain). The maximum supported NUMA node count is 8 (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes`, line 41 of `topology_manager.go`) due to state-space explosion in hint enumeration.\n\n### 2.10 Device Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`, `endpoint.go`, `pod_devices.go`\n\nManages the Device Plugin API. Device plugins register themselves by connecting to the kubelet's plugin watcher socket. The device manager:\n\n- Tracks healthy and unhealthy devices per resource name in `healthyDevices` and `unhealthyDevices` maps.\n- During pod admission, calls `Allocate` on device plugin gRPC endpoints to reserve devices.\n- Returns `RunContainerOptions` (devices, mounts, environment variables, annotations, CDI device IDs) for injection into container configuration via `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions`.\n- Checkpoints allocated device-to-container mappings to survive kubelet restarts.\n- Pushes `resourceupdates.Update` events when device health changes, enabling the kubelet to refresh pod status.\n\nThe device manager also implements `topologymanager.HintProvider`, contributing NUMA node affinity hints based on which NUMA node a physical device is attached to.\n\n### 2.11 DRA Manager\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`, `claiminfo.go`, `healthinfo.go`\n\nThe Dynamic Resource Allocation manager handles `ResourceClaim` objects \u2014 a newer, more expressive alternative to the Device Plugin API, gated by the `DynamicResourceAllocation` feature flag. Unlike device plugins, DRA drivers communicate via structured protobuf API calls rather than environment variables and device file paths.\n\n`PrepareDynamicResources` and `UnprepareDynamicResources` are called by the kubelet's pod lifecycle before and after containers run. Claim state is checkpointed to `{kubeletRootDir}/dra_manager_state`. When the `ResourceHealthStatus` feature gate is also enabled, the DRA manager sends health update events through its `Updates()` channel, which is merged into the container manager's fan-in `resourceUpdates` channel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Initialization\n\n```\nkubelet.go: NewMainKubelet()\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 cm.NewContainerManager(ctx, mountUtil, cadvisor, nodeConfig, ...)\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 GetCgroupSubsystems()   \u2192 detects mounted cgroup hierarchies\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 swap.IsSwapOn()         \u2192 decides if swap should fail or warn\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 cadvisor.MachineInfo()  \u2192 CPU topology, memory, NUMA nodes\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 NewCgroupManager()      \u2192 selects cgroupfs/systemd driver, v1/v2\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 NewQOSContainerManager() \u2192 sets up burstable/besteffort cgroup info\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 topologymanager.NewManager() \u2192 reads NUMA topology, creates scope/policy\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 devicemanager.NewManagerImpl() \u2192 registers as topology hint provider\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 dra.NewManager()        \u2192 (if DynamicResourceAllocation gate enabled)\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpumanager.NewManager() \u2192 loads state checkpoint, registers as hint provider\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 memorymanager.NewManager() \u2192 loads state checkpoint, registers as hint provider\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 starts goroutine fan-in for resourceUpdates channel\n```\n\n### 3.2 Node Setup (Start)\n\n```\nkubelet.go: Run() \u2192 containerManager.Start(ctx, node, activePods, ...)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime() \u2192 snapshot running containers from CRI\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 draManager.Start()      \u2192 begins reconcile loop for ResourceClaims\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.Start()      \u2192 restores allocations from checkpoint, starts reconcile goroutine\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.Start()   \u2192 restores allocations from checkpoint, starts reconcile goroutine\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 cadvisor.RootFsInfo()   \u2192 populates ephemeral storage capacity\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 validateNodeAllocatable() \u2192 sanity-check reserved vs. total resources\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 setupNode(ctx, activePods):\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 validateSystemRequirements() \u2192 checks required cgroup subsystems are mounted\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 setupKernelTunables()  \u2192 vm.overcommit_memory, kernel.panic, etc.\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 createNodeAllocatableCgroups() \u2192 ensures kubepods cgroup exists\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 qosContainerManager.Start() \u2192 creates burstable/besteffort tier cgroups\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups() \u2192 applies limits on kubepods, kube-reserved, system-reserved\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 configures systemContainers (system cgroup, kubelet cgroup OOM score)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.Start()   \u2192 starts gRPC plugin server, registers watcher handler\n```\n\n### 3.3 Pod Admission\n\nWhen the kubelet's predicate admission handler fires (in `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`), the topology manager's `Admit` method runs as a `PodAdmitHandler`:\n\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 for each HintProvider (cpuManager, memoryManager, deviceManager):\n  \u2502     GetTopologyHints(pod, container) \u2192 []TopologyHint (NUMA bitmasks + preferred flag)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 mergeTopologyHints() \u2192 select best affinity per configured policy\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 store affinity per (podUID, containerName)\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 for each HintProvider:\n        Allocate(pod, container) \u2192 reserve resources consistent with chosen affinity\n              cpuManager:    assign CPU set in state (not yet applied to container)\n              memoryManager: assign memory block in state\n              deviceManager: call device plugin Allocate gRPC\n```\n\nIf the policy is `restricted` or `single-numa-node` and no feasible NUMA alignment exists, `Admit` returns a rejection with type `TopologyAffinityError`.\n\nFor DRA resources, `PrepareDynamicResources` is called separately by the pod worker before containers start.\n\n### 3.4 Container Start\n\n```\nkuberuntime_container.go: startContainer(pod, container)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 internalLifecycle.PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity()        \u2192 write cpuset_cpus into ContainerConfig\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() \u2192 write cpuset_mems into ContainerConfig\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 draManager.GetResources()                    \u2192 CDI device IDs\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() \u2192 devices, mounts, envs, CDI\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 podContainerManager.EnsureExists(pod)  \u2192 create/verify pod cgroup\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 CRI: CreateContainer(containerConfig)  \u2190 CPU/memory affinity already embedded\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 internalLifecycle.PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.AddContainer()     \u2192 register containerID \u2192 (podUID, name) mapping\n  \u2502     \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.AddContainer()  \u2192 same\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologyManager.AddContainer() \u2192 same\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 CRI: StartContainer(containerID)\n```\n\n### 3.5 Container Removal\n\n```\nkuberuntime_container.go: killContainer(containerID)\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 CRI: StopContainer()\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 internalLifecycle.PostStopContainer(containerID)\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologyManager.RemoveContainer() \u2192 frees NUMA affinity record\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.RemoveContainer()    \u2192 returns CPUs to shared pool\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.RemoveContainer() \u2192 returns memory blocks to pool\n```\n\nThe pod cgroup is cleaned up asynchronously via `podContainerManager.Destroy()` after all containers in the pod have stopped.\n\n### 3.6 Resource Status Updates\n\nDevice health changes (a device going offline or recovering) propagate via:\n\n```\ndeviceManager updates channel\n  \u2192 containerManagerImpl.resourceUpdates channel (buffered, capacity 10)\n    \u2192 kubelet sync loop\n      \u2192 podStatusManager updates pod status\n```\n\nDRA health events follow the same path when `ResourceHealthStatus` is enabled.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Startup failures that kill the kubelet\n\n`containerManager.Start` failures cause `os.Exit(1)` in the kubelet (`kubelet.go`, line 1755). Conditions that cause this include:\n\n- Required cgroup subsystems (`cpu`, `cpuacct`, `cpuset`, `memory` on v1) are not mounted.\n- The cgroup root specified by `--cgroup-root` does not exist or is invalid.\n- Swap is on and `--fail-swap-on` is true.\n- CPU manager or memory manager fail to restore from checkpoint (e.g., corrupted state file).\n\n### Soft requirements\n\nIf CPU hard-capping (CFS quota) is not available (v1 without `cpu.cfs_quota_us`), `containerManagerImpl.status.SoftRequirements` is set to a non-nil error. The kubelet continues, but CPU limits on containers become advisory-only.\n\n### cgroup v1 deprecation\n\nSince v1 support is explicitly deprecated, `container_manager.go` (lines 51\u201358) defines warning constants (`CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning`, `CgroupV2KernelWarning`) and the Linux container manager emits them at startup. Nodes still on v1 should be migrated to cgroup v2.\n\n### Topology manager NUMA node limit\n\nThe topology manager caps supported NUMA nodes at 8 (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes`, `topology_manager.go` line 41). Beyond that, the combinatorial space of possible NUMA bitmasks becomes too large. On machines with more NUMA nodes the topology manager refuses to start, blocking kubelet startup if the topology manager policy is not `none`.\n\n### CPU manager reconciliation gap\n\nBetween container admission (when the CPU set is written to in-memory state) and `PreStartContainer` (when the container ID is registered), there is a window where the cpuset is not yet applied to the live container process. The reconcile loop closes this gap but introduces a latency equal to `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` (default 10 seconds) for out-of-sync detection.\n\n### Device plugin disconnect\n\nWhen a device plugin disconnects, the device manager marks its devices as unhealthy but retains the endpoint record. Pods that already hold allocations from a disconnected plugin are not immediately evicted, but new pods cannot request that resource type until the plugin reconnects. If the plugin does not reconnect within the kubelet's endpoint stale-detection window, its entries are purged from the checkpoint.\n\n### QoS cgroup memory update retry loop\n\nWhen `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups` cannot apply memory limits immediately (because existing pod memory usage exceeds the new limit), it retries in a goroutine indefinitely with a 1-minute sleep (`node_container_manager_linux.go`, lines 95\u2013107). There is no circuit breaker or alertable metric on this path; monitoring requires watching for `FailedNodeAllocatableEnforcement` / `SuccessfulNodeAllocatableEnforcement` events on the Node object.\n\n### Tradeoff: `CgroupsPerQOS = false`\n\nWith `CgroupsPerQOS: false`, the QoS cgroup tier does not exist and `NewPodContainerManager()` returns the `podContainerManagerNoop` stub. This removes the ability to enforce per-QoS memory reservations but eliminates cgroup management overhead, which can matter on nodes hosting very large numbers of short-lived pods.\n\n### Tradeoff: Static vs. dynamic resource allocation\n\nThe Device Plugin API (device manager) pushes environment variables and device mounts into containers \u2014 a model that is simple but hard to extend. DRA was designed to replace it with a more structured, declarative claim model. Both coexist in the same `containerManagerImpl` today, and `GetResources` (line 729) merges results from both. The fan-in goroutines and dual checkpoints add complexity but allow a staged migration.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policies\n\n**Interface:** `cpumanager.Policy` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go`)\n\nThe `Policy` interface (`Name`, `Start`, `Allocate`, `RemoveContainer`, `GetTopologyHints`, `GetPodTopologyHints`, `GetAllocatableCPUs`) is the intended extension point for custom CPU allocation strategies. The `static` policy supports named options (`CPUManagerPolicyOptions`) such as `full-pcpus-only` and `distribute-cpus-across-numa`, activated at kubelet startup. New options are guarded by per-option validation in `policy_options.go`.\n\n**Risk:** A policy that mismanages state (e.g., double-frees CPU sets or fails to checkpoint) will corrupt the in-memory cpuset assignment and may cause containers to compete for the same physical CPUs.\n\n### 5.2 Memory Manager Policies\n\n**Interface:** `memorymanager.Manager` and embedded `Policy` type\n\nAnalogous to the CPU manager. The `None` policy is a pass-through. The `Static` policy enforces NUMA memory affinity for Guaranteed pods. A new policy must implement the same `Start`/`Allocate`/`RemoveContainer`/`GetTopologyHints` pattern.\n\n### 5.3 Topology Manager Policies and Scopes\n\n**Files:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_*.go`, `scope_*.go`\n\nFour policies and two scopes are selectable at runtime via `--topology-manager-policy` and `--topology-manager-scope`. Policies can also accept per-option maps (`TopologyManagerPolicyOptions`). Adding a new policy means implementing the `Policy` interface and registering it in `NewManager`. Incorrect policy logic that ignores `Preferred: false` hints can silently relax NUMA constraints, degrading memory bandwidth without producing errors.\n\n### 5.4 Device Plugin Registration\n\nThe device manager exposes a gRPC plugin server. Device plugins register at runtime by connecting to the kubelet's plugin socket \u2014 no code changes inside the container manager are required. The device manager's watcher handler is returned by `cm.GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` and integrated into the kubelet's plugin manager subsystem.\n\n**Risk:** A device plugin that incorrectly reports topology (wrong NUMA node affiliation) causes the topology manager to make suboptimal or invalid NUMA alignments for all workloads requesting that device on the node.\n\n### 5.5 DRA Driver Registration\n\nDRA drivers register via `pluginwatcherapi.DRAPlugin`. The `draManager.GetWatcherHandler()` implements the same `cache.PluginHandler` interface used by device plugins, so the existing plugin infrastructure routes registrations to the DRA manager transparently.\n\n### 5.6 Kernel Tunable Behavior\n\n`setupKernelTunables` accepts a `KernelTunableBehavior` enum (`warn`, `error`, `modify`, defined lines 451\u2013454 of `container_manager_linux.go`). The default is `modify` (the kubelet adjusts sysctls like `vm.overcommit_memory`). Setting `--protect-kernel-defaults` switches the behavior to `error`, blocking kubelet startup if host kernel parameters deviate from expected values. This is useful for hardened production environments.\n\n### 5.7 `containerManagerStub` for Testing\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go`\n\nA full no-op implementation used in unit tests and the hollow kubelet (`pkg/kubemark`). It initializes fake CPU and memory managers (`cpumanager.NewFakeManager`, `memorymanager.NewFakeManager`) so `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks can execute without panicking. Factory functions `NewStubContainerManager`, `NewStubContainerManagerWithExtendedResource`, and `NewStubContainerManagerWithDevicePluginResource` let tests control specific behavior.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Platform Variance\n\n### Linux (primary, `//go:build linux`)\n\nFull functionality. The `containerManagerImpl` struct in `container_manager_linux.go` implements the complete `ContainerManager` interface:\n\n- cgroup v1 or v2 hierarchy via `cgroupV1impl` / `cgroupV2impl`\n- QoS cgroup tiers and per-pod cgroups\n- CPU manager with `static` policy (CPU pinning via cpuset)\n- Memory manager with NUMA affinity\n- Topology manager\n- Device manager with device plugin API\n- DRA manager (feature gated)\n- Kernel tunable management\n- OOM score adjustment for the kubelet process (`ensureProcessInContainerWithOOMScore`, line 794)\n\n**cgroup v2 specifics:** The v2 manager (`cgroupV2impl`) uses the unified hierarchy under `/sys/fs/cgroup`. Memory QoS (`MemoryQoS` feature gate) is only meaningful on v2 and uses `memory.min` (guaranteed minimum) and `memory.high` (soft limit). CPU quota uses `cpu.max` (a single `quota period` format) rather than two separate v1 files (`cpu.cfs_quota_us`, `cpu.cfs_period_us`).\n\n### Windows (`//go:build windows`)\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go`\n\nThe Windows `containerManagerImpl` contains `deviceManager`, `topologyManager`, `cpuManager`, and `memoryManager` fields. Device plugin and topology-aware resource allocation therefore function on Windows. However, there is no cgroup infrastructure: QoS containers, pod cgroups, and node allocatable enforcement are absent. Methods like `GetQOSContainersInfo`, `GetMountedSubsystems`, and `GetPodCgroupRoot` return empty or stub values. The `InternalContainerLifecycle` Windows implementation (`internal_container_lifecycle_windows.go`) has an empty `PreCreateContainer` \u2014 CPU/memory affinity cannot be injected at the container-config level on Windows.\n\n### Stub / unsupported platforms\n\n**File:** `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go` (used on non-Linux, non-Windows in tests), `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_unsupported.go` (returns error from `NewContainerManager` on other platforms)\n\nThe stub satisfies the full `ContainerManager` interface with no-op implementations, enabling unit tests on any host OS.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**cgroup write overhead:** Every pod start triggers at minimum one `cgroupManager.Create` call (pod cgroup) plus `cgroupManager.Update` calls for the QoS tier recalculation. On nodes with many short-lived pods (batch workloads), this can become measurable I/O contention on the cgroup filesystem. The v2 unified hierarchy reduces per-operation syscalls compared to v1, which requires one write per subsystem mount.\n\n**CPU manager reconciliation:** The reconcile loop calls `UpdateContainerResources` on the CRI for every container that has drifted from its expected cpuset. On nodes with many Guaranteed pods, this loop can issue hundreds of CRI calls per reconcile period. Tuning `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` higher reduces overhead but increases the window in which a container runs on wrong CPUs after a restart.\n\n**Topology hint computation cost:** At pod admission, the topology manager collects hints from all providers and computes their intersection. The cost grows combinatorially with NUMA node count. For the common case (2\u20134 NUMA nodes, 3 providers) this is sub-millisecond, but it becomes a bottleneck on 8-node NUMA machines under heavy admission pressure.\n\n### Reliability\n\n**Checkpoint durability:** CPU manager, memory manager, and device manager all checkpoint allocation state to files under `KubeletRootDir`. If that directory is on a volatile tmpfs (e.g., during testing or misconfigured deployments), the managers cannot reconcile pre-existing allocations after a kubelet restart and may over-allocate or under-allocate resources. Best practice is to use a persistent `--root-dir`.\n\n**QoS cgroup update retry loop:** The node allocatable enforcement goroutine (`enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups`) silently retries indefinitely with no circuit breaker or counter-metric. Operators must monitor the Node event stream for `FailedNodeAllocatableEnforcement` and `SuccessfulNodeAllocatableEnforcement` event reasons to detect this condition.\n\n**Resource update channel back-pressure:** The `resourceUpdates` channel between device/DRA managers and the kubelet's sync loop is buffered at capacity 10 (`container_manager_linux.go`, line 360). If the kubelet's main sync loop is stalled (slow API server, high pod churn), this channel can fill and cause goroutines in the fan-in loop to block, delaying health status propagation.\n\n### Maintainability\n\nThe Linux implementation couples three distinct concerns in one 1100+ line `containerManagerImpl`: cgroup hierarchy management, resource manager lifecycle, and node allocatable accounting. An acknowledged TODO at line 728 (`// TODO: move the GetResources logic to PodContainerManager`) reflects this debt. The initialization order dependency \u2014 topology manager must precede all hint providers \u2014 is implicit and not enforced by the type system, making refactoring risky.\n\nThe use of build tags (`//go:build linux`, `//go:build windows`) for platform variance, rather than interface dispatch, means adding a new platform requires duplicating struct definitions and all method bodies. The Windows and stub implementations already diverge significantly in what sub-managers they initialize, and there is no shared base type to enforce consistency.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | `ContainerManager` interface; `NodeConfig`; helper functions for resource parsing and device topology serialization |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux `containerManagerImpl`; `NewContainerManager`; `Start`; fan-in of resource update channels; per-container resource helpers |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows `containerManagerImpl`; partial implementation (no cgroup hierarchy) |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go` | No-op stub for tests and hollow kubelet; `NewStubContainerManager` and variants |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | `CgroupManager`, `PodContainerManager`, `QOSContainersInfo`, `ResourceConfig`, `CgroupConfig`, `CgroupName` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` | `CgroupName` path conversion (cgroupfs and systemd); `NewCgroupManager`; shared v1/v2 logic |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` | cgroup v1 implementation of `CgroupManager` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` | cgroup v2 implementation of `CgroupManager` (`cgroupV2impl`); `memory.max`, `cpu.max`, `cpu.weight` |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` | `QOSContainerManager`; burstable/besteffort tier creation; periodic QoS cgroup update |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` | `podContainerManagerImpl`; NUMA node limit constant |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/scope.go` | `Scope` interface; admission orchestration across hint providers |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_*.go` | `none`, `best-effort`, `restricted`, `single-numa-node` policy implementations |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go` | `ManagerImpl`;
